For the eponymous character, see <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(literary_character)" title="James Bond (literary character)">James Bond (literary character)</a>. For the ornithologist, see <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(ornithologist)" title="James Bond (ornithologist)">James Bond (ornithologist)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="James Bond (disambiguation)">James Bond (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"007" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/007_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="007 (disambiguation)">007 (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-style: italic; background: lavender;">James Bond</th></tr><tr><td class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pierce_Brosnan" title="Pierce Brosnan">Pierce Brosnan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Craig" title="Daniel Craig">Daniel Craig</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timothy_Dalton" title="Timothy Dalton">Timothy Dalton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Holness" title="Bob Holness">Bob Holness</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Jayston" title="Michael Jayston">Michael Jayston</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Lazenby" title="George Lazenby">George Lazenby</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roger_Moore" title="Roger Moore">Roger Moore</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Barry_Nelson" title="Barry Nelson">Barry Nelson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/David_Niven" title="David Niven">David Niven</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Toby_Stephens" title="Toby Stephens">Toby Stephens</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <i><b>James Bond</b></i> series focuses on a fictional <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">British Secret Service</a> agent created in 1953 by writer <a href="/wiki/Ian_Fleming" title="Ian Fleming">Ian Fleming</a>, who featured him in twelve novels and two short-story collections. Since Fleming\'s death in 1964, eight other authors have written authorised Bond novels or novelizations: <a href="/wiki/Kingsley_Amis" title="Kingsley Amis">Kingsley Amis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wood_(writer)" title="Christopher Wood (writer)">Christopher Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Gardner_(British_writer)" title="John Gardner (British writer)">John Gardner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Benson" title="Raymond Benson">Raymond Benson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Faulks" title="Sebastian Faulks">Sebastian Faulks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffery_Deaver" title="Jeffery Deaver">Jeffery Deaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Boyd_(writer)" title="William Boyd (writer)">William Boyd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Horowitz" title="Anthony Horowitz">Anthony Horowitz</a>. The latest novel is <i><a href="/wiki/Trigger_Mortis" title="Trigger Mortis">Trigger Mortis</a></i> by Anthony Horowitz, published in September 2015. Additionally <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Higson" title="Charlie Higson">Charlie Higson</a> wrote a series on <a href="/wiki/Young_Bond" title="Young Bond">a young James Bond</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Weinberg" title="Samantha Weinberg">Kate Westbrook</a> wrote three novels based on the <a href="/wiki/The_Moneypenny_Diaries" title="The Moneypenny Diaries">diaries of a recurring series character</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miss_Moneypenny" title="Miss Moneypenny">Moneypenny</a>.\n</p><p>The character has also been adapted for television, radio, comic strip, video games and film. The films are the longest continually running film series of all time and have grossed over $7.040 billion in total, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films#Highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" title="List of highest-grossing films">fourth-highest-grossing film series</a> to date, which started in 1962 with <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)">Dr. No</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> as Bond. As of 2018, there have been twenty-four films in the <a href="/wiki/Eon_Productions" title="Eon Productions">Eon Productions</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">series</a>. The most recent Bond film, <i><a href="/wiki/Spectre_(2015_film)" title="Spectre (2015 film)">Spectre</a></i> (2015), stars <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Craig" title="Daniel Craig">Daniel Craig</a> in his fourth portrayal of Bond; he is the sixth actor to play Bond in the Eon series. There have also been two independent productions of Bond films: <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(1967_film)" title="Casino Royale (1967 film)">Casino Royale</a></i> (a 1967 <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">spoof</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Say_Never_Again" title="Never Say Never Again">Never Say Never Again</a></i> (a 1983 remake of an earlier Eon-produced film, <i><a href="/wiki/Thunderball_(film)" title="Thunderball (film)">Thunderball</a></i>). In 2015 the series was estimated to be worth $19.9 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> making <i>James Bond</i> one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_highest-grossing_media_franchises" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the highest-grossing media franchises">highest-grossing media franchises of all time</a>.\n</p><p>The Bond films are renowned for a number of features, including the musical accompaniment, with the theme songs having received <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominations on several occasions, and two wins. Other important elements which run through most of the films include Bond\'s cars, his guns, and the gadgets with which he is supplied by <a href="/wiki/Q_(James_Bond)" title="Q (James Bond)">Q Branch</a>. The films are also noted for Bond\'s relationships with various women, who are sometimes referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Bond_girl" title="Bond girl">Bond girls</a>".\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Publication_history">Publication history</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_and_inspiration">Creation and inspiration</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(literary_character)" title="James Bond (literary character)">James Bond (literary character)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inspirations_for_James_Bond" title="Inspirations for James Bond">Inspirations for James Bond</a></div>\n<p>Ian Fleming created the fictional character of James Bond as the central figure for his works. Bond is an intelligence officer in the <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">Secret Intelligence Service</a>, commonly known as MI6. Bond is known by his code number, 007, and was a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Reserve" title="Royal Naval Reserve">Royal Naval Reserve</a> <a href="/wiki/Commander_(Royal_Navy)" title="Commander (Royal Navy)">Commander</a>. Fleming based his fictional creation on a number of individuals he came across during his time in the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Intelligence_Division" title="Naval Intelligence Division">Naval Intelligence Division</a> during the Second World War, admitting that Bond "was a compound of all the secret agents and commando types I met during the war".<sup id="cite_ref-Macintyre_(2008)_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macintyre_(2008)-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Among those types were his brother, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Fleming_(writer)" title="Peter Fleming (writer)">Peter</a>, who had been involved in behind-the-lines operations in <a href="/wiki/Norway_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Norway in World War II">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Greece in World War II">Greece</a> during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-PF_Obit_(1971)_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PF_Obit_(1971)-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Aside from Fleming\'s brother, a number of others also provided some aspects of Bond\'s make up, including <a href="/wiki/Conrad_O%27Brien-ffrench" title="Conrad O&#39;Brien-ffrench">Conrad O\'Brien-ffrench</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Dalzel-Job" title="Patrick Dalzel-Job">Patrick Dalzel-Job</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Dunderdale" title="Wilfred Dunderdale">Bill "Biffy" Dunderdale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Macintyre_(2008)_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macintyre_(2008)-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name James Bond came from that of the American <a href="/wiki/Ornithologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ornithologist">ornithologist</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(ornithologist)" title="James Bond (ornithologist)">James Bond</a>, a Caribbean bird expert and author of the definitive <a href="/wiki/Field_guide" title="Field guide">field guide</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Birds_of_the_West_Indies" title="Birds of the West Indies">Birds of the West Indies</a></i>. Fleming, a keen <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatcher</a> himself, had a copy of Bond\'s guide and he later explained to the ornithologist\'s wife that "It struck me that this brief, unromantic, Anglo-Saxon and yet very masculine name was just what I needed, and so a second James Bond was born".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaplen201021_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaplen201021-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He further explained that:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>When I wrote the first one in 1953, I wanted Bond to be an extremely dull, uninteresting man to whom things happened; I wanted him to be a blunt instrument&#160;... when I was casting around for a name for my protagonist I thought by God, [James Bond] is the dullest name I ever heard.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Ian Fleming, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i>, 21 April 1962<sup id="cite_ref-Hellman_(1962)_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hellman_(1962)-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>On another occasion, Fleming said: "I wanted the simplest, dullest, plainest-sounding name I could find, \'James Bond\' was much better than something more interesting, like \'Peregrine Carruthers\'. Exotic things would happen to and around him, but he would be a neutral figure\xe2\x80\x94an anonymous, blunt instrument wielded by a government department."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor2005112_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor2005112-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg/170px-Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg/255px-Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg/340px-Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoagy_Carmichael_-_1947.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hoagy_Carmichael" title="Hoagy Carmichael">Hoagy Carmichael</a>\xe2\x80\x94Fleming\'s view of James Bond</div></div></div>\n<p>Fleming decided that Bond should resemble both American singer <a href="/wiki/Hoagy_Carmichael" title="Hoagy Carmichael">Hoagy Carmichael</a> and himself<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre200867_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre200867-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(novel)" title="Casino Royale (novel)"><i>Casino Royale</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Vesper_Lynd" title="Vesper Lynd">Vesper Lynd</a> remarks, "Bond reminds me rather of Hoagy Carmichael, but there is something cold and ruthless." Likewise, in <a href="/wiki/Moonraker_(novel)" title="Moonraker (novel)"><i>Moonraker</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_Branch" title="Special Branch">Special Branch</a> Officer <a href="/wiki/Gala_Brand" class="mw-redirect" title="Gala Brand">Gala Brand</a> thinks that Bond is "certainly good-looking&#160;... Rather like Hoagy Carmichael in a way. That black hair falling down over the right eyebrow. Much the same bones. But there was something a bit cruel in the mouth, and the eyes were cold."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre200867_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre200867-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fleming endowed Bond with many of his own traits, including sharing the same golf handicap, the taste for scrambled eggs and using the same brand of toiletries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre200850_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre200850-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Bond\'s tastes are also often taken from Fleming\'s own as was his behaviour,<sup id="cite_ref-Cook_(2004)_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook_(2004)-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> with Bond\'s love of golf and gambling mirroring Fleming\'s own. Fleming used his experiences of his espionage career and all other aspects of his life as inspiration when writing, including using names of school friends, acquaintances, relatives and lovers throughout his books.<sup id="cite_ref-Macintyre_(2008)_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macintyre_(2008)-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was not until the penultimate novel, <i><a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(novel)" title="You Only Live Twice (novel)">You Only Live Twice</a></i>, that Fleming gave Bond a sense of family background. The book was the first to be written after the release of <a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)"><i>Dr. No</i></a> in cinemas and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a>\'s depiction of Bond affected Fleming\'s interpretation of the character, to give Bond both a sense of humour and Scottish antecedents that were not present in the previous stories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008205_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008205-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In a fictional obituary, purportedly published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, Bond\'s parents were given as Andrew Bond, from the village of <a href="/wiki/Glencoe,_Highland" title="Glencoe, Highland">Glencoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, and Monique Delacroix, from the canton of <a href="/wiki/Vaud" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaud">Vaud</a>, Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor200559_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor200559-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Fleming did not provide Bond\'s date of birth, but <a href="/wiki/John_Pearson_(author)" title="John Pearson (author)">John Pearson</a>\'s fictional biography of Bond, <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond:_The_Authorized_Biography_of_007" title="James Bond: The Authorized Biography of 007">James Bond: The Authorized Biography of 007</a></i>, gives Bond a birth date on 11 November 1920,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPearson200821_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPearson200821-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> while a study by John Griswold puts the date at 11 November 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriswold200627_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriswold200627-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novels_and_related_works">Novels and related works</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_James_Bond_novels_and_short_stories" title="List of James Bond novels and short stories">List of James Bond novels and short stories</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ian_Fleming_novels">Ian Fleming novels</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GoldeneyeEstate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/GoldeneyeEstate.jpg/220px-GoldeneyeEstate.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/GoldeneyeEstate.jpg/330px-GoldeneyeEstate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/GoldeneyeEstate.jpg/440px-GoldeneyeEstate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="654" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GoldeneyeEstate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Goldeneye_(estate)" title="Goldeneye (estate)">Goldeneye</a>, in Jamaica, where Fleming wrote all the Bond novels<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008208_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008208-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Whilst serving in the Naval Intelligence Division, Fleming had planned to become an author<sup id="cite_ref-Lycett_(DNB)_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lycett_(DNB)-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and had told a friend, "I am going to write the spy story to end all spy stories."<sup id="cite_ref-Macintyre_(2008)_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macintyre_(2008)-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> On 17 February 1952, he began writing his first James Bond novel, <i>Casino Royale</i>, at his <a href="/wiki/Goldeneye_(estate)" title="Goldeneye (estate)">Goldeneye estate</a> in Jamaica,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor20054_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor20054-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> where he wrote all his Bond novels during the months of January and February each year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor20055_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor20055-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He started the story shortly before his wedding to his pregnant girlfriend, Ann Charteris, in order to distract himself from his forthcoming nuptials.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBennettWoollacott20031ch_1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBennettWoollacott20031ch_1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After completing the manuscript for <i>Casino Royale</i>, Fleming showed the manuscript to his friend (and later editor) <a href="/wiki/William_Plomer" title="William Plomer">William Plomer</a> to read. Plomer liked it and submitted it to the publishers, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Cape" title="Jonathan Cape">Jonathan Cape</a>, who did not like it as much. Cape finally published it in 1953 on the recommendation of Fleming\'s older brother <a href="/wiki/Peter_Fleming_(writer)" title="Peter Fleming (writer)">Peter</a>, an established travel writer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor20055_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor20055-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Between 1953 and 1966, two years after his death, twelve novels and two short-story collections were published, with the last two books \xe2\x80\x93 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Golden_Gun_(novel)" title="The Man with the Golden Gun (novel)">The Man with the Golden Gun</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Octopussy_and_The_Living_Daylights" title="Octopussy and The Living Daylights">Octopussy and The Living Daylights</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 published posthumously.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack200575_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack200575-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> All the books were published in the UK through Jonathan Cape.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top; width:225px;">\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>1953 <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(novel)" title="Casino Royale (novel)">Casino Royale</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1954 <i><a href="/wiki/Live_and_Let_Die_(novel)" title="Live and Let Die (novel)">Live and Let Die</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1955 <i><a href="/wiki/Moonraker_(novel)" title="Moonraker (novel)">Moonraker</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1956 <i><a href="/wiki/Diamonds_Are_Forever_(novel)" title="Diamonds Are Forever (novel)">Diamonds Are Forever</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1957 <i><a href="/wiki/From_Russia,_with_Love_(novel)" title="From Russia, with Love (novel)">From Russia, with Love</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1958 <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(novel)" title="Dr. No (novel)">Dr. No</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1959 <i><a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(novel)" title="Goldfinger (novel)">Goldfinger</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</td>\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>1960 <i><a href="/wiki/For_Your_Eyes_Only_(short_story_collection)" title="For Your Eyes Only (short story collection)">For Your Eyes Only</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> (short stories)</li>\n<li>1961 <i><a href="/wiki/Thunderball_(novel)" title="Thunderball (novel)">Thunderball</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1962 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spy_Who_Loved_Me_(novel)" title="The Spy Who Loved Me (novel)">The Spy Who Loved Me</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1963 <i><a href="/wiki/On_Her_Majesty%27s_Secret_Service_(novel)" title="On Her Majesty&#39;s Secret Service (novel)">On Her Majesty\'s Secret Service</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1964 <i><a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(novel)" title="You Only Live Twice (novel)">You Only Live Twice</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1965 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Golden_Gun_(novel)" title="The Man with the Golden Gun (novel)">The Man with the Golden Gun</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1966 <i><a href="/wiki/Octopussy_and_The_Living_Daylights" title="Octopussy and The Living Daylights">Octopussy and The Living Daylights</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> (short stories; "The Property of a Lady" added to subsequent editions)</li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Fleming_novels">Post-Fleming novels</span></h4>\n<p>After Fleming\'s death a continuation novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Colonel_Sun" title="Colonel Sun">Colonel Sun</a></i>, was written by <a href="/wiki/Kingsley_Amis" title="Kingsley Amis">Kingsley Amis</a> (as <a href="/wiki/Robert_Markham" title="Robert Markham">Robert Markham</a>) and published in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Amis had already written a literary study of Fleming\'s Bond novels in his 1965 work <i><a href="/wiki/The_James_Bond_Dossier" title="The James Bond Dossier">The James Bond Dossier</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198832_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198832-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Novelization" title="Novelization">novelizations</a> of two of the <a href="/wiki/Eon_Productions" title="Eon Productions">Eon Productions</a> Bond films appeared in print, <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond,_The_Spy_Who_Loved_Me" title="James Bond, The Spy Who Loved Me">James Bond, The Spy Who Loved Me</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_and_Moonraker" title="James Bond and Moonraker">James Bond and Moonraker</a></i>, both written by screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wood_(writer)" title="Christopher Wood (writer)">Christopher Wood</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-IFP,_Novelizations_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFP,_Novelizations-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> the series of novels did not continue until the 1980s. In 1981 the thriller writer <a href="/wiki/John_Gardner_(British_writer)" title="John Gardner (British writer)">John Gardner</a> picked up the series with <i><a href="/wiki/Licence_Renewed" title="Licence Renewed">Licence Renewed</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200258_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200258-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Gardner went on to write sixteen Bond books in total; two of the books he wrote \xe2\x80\x93 <i><a href="/wiki/Licence_to_Kill" title="Licence to Kill">Licence to Kill</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/GoldenEye" title="GoldenEye">GoldenEye</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 were novelizations of Eon Productions films of the same name. Gardner moved the Bond series into the 1980s, although he retained the ages of the characters as they were when Fleming had left them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson1988149_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson1988149-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In 1996 Gardner retired from writing James Bond books due to ill health.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top; width:225px;">\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>1981 <i><a href="/wiki/Licence_Renewed" title="Licence Renewed">Licence Renewed</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1982 <i><a href="/wiki/For_Special_Services" title="For Special Services">For Special Services</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1983 <i><a href="/wiki/Icebreaker_(novel)" title="Icebreaker (novel)">Icebreaker</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1984 <i><a href="/wiki/Role_of_Honour" title="Role of Honour">Role of Honour</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1986 <i><a href="/wiki/Nobody_Lives_for_Ever" title="Nobody Lives for Ever">Nobody Lives for Ever</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1987 <i><a href="/wiki/No_Deals,_Mr._Bond" title="No Deals, Mr. Bond">No Deals, Mr. Bond</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1988 <i><a href="/wiki/Scorpius_(novel)" title="Scorpius (novel)">Scorpius</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1989 <i><a href="/wiki/Win,_Lose_or_Die" title="Win, Lose or Die">Win, Lose or Die</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</td>\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>1989 <i>Licence to Kill</i><sup id="cite_ref-IFP,_Novelizations_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFP,_Novelizations-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> (novelization)</li>\n<li>1990 <i><a href="/wiki/Brokenclaw" title="Brokenclaw">Brokenclaw</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1991 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_from_Barbarossa" title="The Man from Barbarossa">The Man from Barbarossa</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1992 <i><a href="/wiki/Death_is_Forever" title="Death is Forever">Death is Forever</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1993 <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Send_Flowers" title="Never Send Flowers">Never Send Flowers</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1994 <i><a href="/wiki/SeaFire" title="SeaFire">SeaFire</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1995 <i>GoldenEye</i><sup id="cite_ref-IFP,_Novelizations_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFP,_Novelizations-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> (novelization)</li>\n<li>1996 <i><a href="/wiki/Cold_(novel)" title="Cold (novel)">Cold</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 1996 the American author <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Benson" title="Raymond Benson">Raymond Benson</a> became the author of the Bond novels. Benson had previously been the author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_James_Bond_Bedside_Companion" title="The James Bond Bedside Companion">The James Bond Bedside Companion</a></i>, first published in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\nBy the time he moved on to other, non-Bond related projects in 2002, Benson had written six Bond novels, three novelizations and three short stories.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top; width:225px;">\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>1997 "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_uncollected_short_stories#&quot;Blast_from_the_Past&quot;" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond uncollected short stories">Blast From the Past</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200262_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200262-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> (short story)</li>\n<li>1997 <i><a href="/wiki/Zero_Minus_Ten" title="Zero Minus Ten">Zero Minus Ten</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1997 <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Dies" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">Tomorrow Never Dies</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-IFP,_Novelizations_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFP,_Novelizations-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> (novelization)</li>\n<li>1998 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Facts_of_Death" title="The Facts of Death">The Facts of Death</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1999 "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_uncollected_short_stories#&quot;Midsummer_Night&#39;s_Doom&quot;" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond uncollected short stories">Midsummer Night\'s Doom</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200263_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200263-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> (short story)</li>\n<li>1999 "<a id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200264_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200264-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> (short story)</li></ul>\n</td>\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>1999 <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough" title="The World Is Not Enough">The World Is Not Enough</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-IFP,_Novelizations_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFP,_Novelizations-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> (novelization)</li>\n<li>1999 <i><a href="/wiki/High_Time_to_Kill" title="High Time to Kill">High Time to Kill</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2000 <i><a href="/wiki/DoubleShot" title="DoubleShot">DoubleShot</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2001 <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Dream_of_Dying" title="Never Dream of Dying">Never Dream of Dying</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2002 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Red_Tattoo" title="The Man with the Red Tattoo">The Man with the Red Tattoo</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2002 <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day" title="Die Another Day">Die Another Day</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-IFP,_Novelizations_36-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFP,_Novelizations-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> (novelization)</li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>After a gap of six years, <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Faulks" title="Sebastian Faulks">Sebastian Faulks</a> was commissioned by Ian Fleming Publications to write a new Bond novel, which was released on 28 May 2008, the 100th anniversary of Fleming\'s birth.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The book\xe2\x80\x94titled <i><a href="/wiki/Devil_May_Care_(Faulks_novel)" title="Devil May Care (Faulks novel)">Devil May Care</a></i>\xe2\x80\x94was published in the UK by Penguin Books and by Doubleday in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Faulks_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faulks-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> American writer <a href="/wiki/Jeffery_Deaver" title="Jeffery Deaver">Jeffery Deaver</a> was then commissioned by Ian Fleming Publications to produce <a href="/wiki/Carte_Blanche_(novel)" title="Carte Blanche (novel)"><i>Carte Blanche</i></a>, which was published on 26 May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The book updated Bond into a post-9/11 agent, independent of <a href="/wiki/MI5" title="MI5">MI5</a> or MI6.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 26 September 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Solo_(Boyd_novel)" title="Solo (Boyd novel)">Solo</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/William_Boyd_(writer)" title="William Boyd (writer)">William Boyd</a>, was published, set in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In October 2014 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Horowitz" title="Anthony Horowitz">Anthony Horowitz</a> was to write a <i>Bond</i> continuation novel.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Set in the 1950s two weeks after the events of <i>Goldfinger</i>, it contains material written, but previously unreleased, by Fleming. <i><a href="/wiki/Trigger_Mortis" title="Trigger Mortis">Trigger Mortis</a></i> was released on 8 September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top; width:225px;">\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>2008 <i><a href="/wiki/Devil_May_Care_(Faulks_novel)" title="Devil May Care (Faulks novel)">Devil May Care</a></i></li>\n<li>2011 <i><a href="/wiki/Carte_Blanche_(novel)" title="Carte Blanche (novel)">Carte Blanche</a></i></li></ul>\n</td>\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Solo_(Boyd_novel)" title="Solo (Boyd novel)">Solo</a></i></li>\n<li>2015 <i><a href="/wiki/Trigger_Mortis" title="Trigger Mortis">Trigger Mortis</a></i></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_Bond">Young Bond</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Young_Bond" title="Young Bond">Young Bond</a></div>\n<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Young_Bond" title="Young Bond">Young Bond</a></i> series of novels was started by <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Higson" title="Charlie Higson">Charlie Higson</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and, between 2005 and 2009, five novels and one short story were published.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The first Young Bond novel, <i><a href="/wiki/SilverFin" title="SilverFin">SilverFin</a></i> was also adapted and released as a graphic novel on 2 October 2008 by Puffin Books.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In October 2013 Ian Fleming Publications announced that <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Cole_(writer)" title="Stephen Cole (writer)">Stephen Cole</a> would continue the series, with the first edition scheduled to be released in Autumn 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align: top;">\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>2005 <i>SilverFin</i><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2006 <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_Fever" title="Blood Fever">Blood Fever</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2007 <i><a href="/wiki/Double_or_Die" title="Double or Die">Double or Die</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2007 <i><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gold" title="Hurricane Gold">Hurricane Gold</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2008 <i><a href="/wiki/By_Royal_Command" title="By Royal Command">By Royal Command</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> &amp; <i>SilverFin</i><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> (graphic novel)</li>\n<li>2009 "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_uncollected_short_stories#&quot;A_Hard_Man_to_Kill&quot;" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond uncollected short stories">A Hard Man to Kill</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> (short story)</li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Moneypenny_Diaries"><i>The Moneypenny Diaries</i></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Moneypenny_Diaries" title="The Moneypenny Diaries">The Moneypenny Diaries</a></div>\n<p><i>The Moneypenny Diaries</i> are a trilogy of novels chronicling the life of <a href="/wiki/Miss_Moneypenny" title="Miss Moneypenny">Miss Moneypenny</a>, <a href="/wiki/M_(James_Bond)" title="M (James Bond)">M</a>\'s personal secretary. The novels are penned by <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Weinberg" title="Samantha Weinberg">Samantha Weinberg</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonym</a> Kate Westbrook, who is depicted as the book\'s "editor".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The first instalment of the trilogy, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Moneypenny_Diaries:_Guardian_Angel" title="The Moneypenny Diaries: Guardian Angel">Guardian Angel</a></i>, was released on 10 October 2005 in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> A second volume, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/Secret_Servant:_The_Moneypenny_Diaries" title="Secret Servant: The Moneypenny Diaries">Secret Servant</a></i> was released on 2 November 2006 in the UK, published by <a href="/wiki/John_Murray_(publisher)" title="John Murray (publisher)">John Murray</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> A third volume, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Moneypenny_Diaries:_Final_Fling" title="The Moneypenny Diaries: Final Fling">Final Fling</a></i> was released on 1 May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top; width:225px;">\n<td style="width:400pt;">\n<ul><li>2005 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Moneypenny_Diaries:_Guardian_Angel" title="The Moneypenny Diaries: Guardian Angel">The Moneypenny Diaries: Guardian Angel</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2006 <i><a href="/wiki/Secret_Servant:_The_Moneypenny_Diaries" title="Secret Servant: The Moneypenny Diaries">Secret Servant: The Moneypenny Diaries</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2008 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Moneypenny_Diaries:_Final_Fling" title="The Moneypenny Diaries: Final Fling">The Moneypenny Diaries: Final Fling</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Adaptations">Adaptations</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span></h3>\n<p>In 1954 <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> paid Ian Fleming $1,000 ($9,113 in 2017 dollars<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-US_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-US-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>) to adapt his novel <a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(novel)" title="Casino Royale (novel)"><i>Casino Royale</i></a> into a one-hour television adventure as part of its <i><a href="/wiki/Climax!" title="Climax!">Climax!</a></i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack200514_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack200514-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The episode aired live on 21 October 1954 and starred <a href="/wiki/Barry_Nelson" title="Barry Nelson">Barry Nelson</a> as "Card Sense" James Bond and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lorre" title="Peter Lorre">Peter Lorre</a> as Le Chiffre.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198811_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198811-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The novel was adapted for American audiences to show Bond as an American agent working for "Combined Intelligence", while the character <a href="/wiki/Felix_Leiter" title="Felix Leiter">Felix Leiter</a>\xe2\x80\x94American in the novel\xe2\x80\x94became British onscreen and was renamed "Clarence Leiter".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2005101_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2005101-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1973 a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Omnibus_(UK_TV_series)" title="Omnibus (UK TV series)">Omnibus</a>: The British Hero</i> featured <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Cazenove" title="Christopher Cazenove">Christopher Cazenove</a> playing a number of such title characters (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hannay" title="Richard Hannay">Richard Hannay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulldog_Drummond" title="Bulldog Drummond">Bulldog Drummond</a>). The documentary included James Bond in dramatised scenes from\n<a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(novel)" title="Goldfinger (novel)"><i>Goldfinger</i></a>\xe2\x80\x94notably featuring 007 being threatened with the novel\'s circular saw, rather than the film\'s laser beam\xe2\x80\x94and <i><a href="/wiki/Diamonds_Are_Forever_(film)" title="Diamonds Are Forever (film)">Diamonds Are Forever</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In 1991 a TV cartoon series <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Jr." title="James Bond Jr.">James Bond Jr.</a></i> was produced with <a href="/wiki/Corey_Burton" title="Corey Burton">Corey Burton</a> in the role of Bond\'s nephew, also called James Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span></h3>\n<p>In 1956 the novel <a href="/wiki/Moonraker_(novel)" title="Moonraker (novel)"><i>Moonraker</i></a> was adapted for broadcast on <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> radio, with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Holness" title="Bob Holness">Bob Holness</a> providing the voice of Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>, "listeners across the Union thrilled to Bob\'s cultured tones as he defeated evil master criminals in search of world domination".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> have adapted five of the Fleming novels for broadcast: in 1990 <a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(novel)" title="You Only Live Twice (novel)"><i>You Only Live Twice</i></a> was adapted into a 90-minute radio play for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a> with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jayston" title="Michael Jayston">Michael Jayston</a> playing James Bond. The production was repeated a number of times between 2008 and 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On 24 May 2008 BBC Radio 4 broadcast an adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(novel)" title="Dr. No (novel)"><i>Dr. No</i></a>. The actor <a href="/wiki/Toby_Stephens" title="Toby Stephens">Toby Stephens</a>, who played Bond villain <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Graves" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustav Graves">Gustav Graves</a> in the Eon Productions version of <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day" title="Die Another Day">Die Another Day</a></i>, played Bond, while Dr. No was played by <a href="/wiki/David_Suchet" title="David Suchet">David Suchet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Following its success, a second story was adapted and on 3 April 2010 <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a> broadcast <a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(novel)" title="Goldfinger (novel)"><i>Goldfinger</i></a> with Stephens again playing Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Sir Ian McKellen</a> was Goldfinger and Stephens\' <i>Die Another Day</i> co-star <a href="/wiki/Rosamund_Pike" title="Rosamund Pike">Rosamund Pike</a> played Pussy Galore. The play was adapted from Fleming\'s novel by Archie Scottney and was directed by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Jarvis_(actor)" title="Martin Jarvis (actor)">Martin Jarvis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2012 the novel <a href="/wiki/From_Russia,_with_Love_(novel)" title="From Russia, with Love (novel)"><i>From Russia, with Love</i></a> was dramatized for Radio 4; it featured a full cast again starring Stephens as Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In May 2014 Stephens again played Bond, in <i><a href="/wiki/On_Her_Majesty%27s_Secret_Service_(novel)" title="On Her Majesty&#39;s Secret Service (novel)">On Her Majesty\'s Secret Service</a></i>, with <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Molina" title="Alfred Molina">Alfred Molina</a> as Blofeld, and <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Lumley" title="Joanna Lumley">Joanna Lumley</a> as Irma Bunt.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comics">Comics</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(comic_strip)" title="James Bond (comic strip)">James Bond (comic strip)</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_comic_books" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond comic books">James Bond comic books</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McLusky007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ac/McLusky007.jpg/170px-McLusky007.jpg" width="170" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ac/McLusky007.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="249" data-file-height="401" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McLusky007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John McLusky\'s rendition of James Bond</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1957 the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Express" title="Daily Express">Daily Express</a></i> approached Ian Fleming to adapt his stories into comic strips, offering him \xc2\xa31,500 per novel and a share of takings from syndication.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting20076_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting20076-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> After initial reluctance, Fleming, who felt the strips would lack the quality of his writing, agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELycett1996316_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELycett1996316-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> To aid the <i>Daily Express</i> in illustrating Bond, Fleming commissioned an artist to create a sketch of how he believed James Bond looked. The illustrator, <a href="/wiki/John_McLusky" title="John McLusky">John McLusky</a>, however, felt that Fleming\'s 007 looked too "outdated" and "pre-war" and changed Bond to give him a more masculine look.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200221_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200221-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The first strip, <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(novel)" title="Casino Royale (novel)">Casino Royale</a></i> was published from 7 July 1958 to 13 December 1958<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlemingGammidgeMcLusky19886_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlemingGammidgeMcLusky19886-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> and was written by Anthony Hern and illustrated by John McLusky.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting20077_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting20077-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the Bond novels and short stories have since been adapted for illustration, as well as Kingsley Amis\'s <i>Colonel Sun</i>; the works were written by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Gammidge" title="Henry Gammidge">Henry Gammidge</a> or Jim Lawrence with <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_Horak" title="Yaroslav Horak">Yaroslav Horak</a> replacing McClusky as artist in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlemingGammidgeMcLusky19886_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlemingGammidgeMcLusky19886-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> After the Fleming and Amis material had been adapted, original stories were produced, continuing in the <i>Daily Express</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday Express">Sunday Express</a></i> until May 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200221_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200221-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> adaptations of the James Bond films have been published through the years: at the time of <a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)"><i>Dr. No</i></a>\'s release in October 1962, a <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> adaptation of the screenplay, written by Norman J. Nodel, was published in Britain as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Classics_Illustrated" title="Classics Illustrated">Classics Illustrated</a></i> anthology series.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> It was later reprinted in the United States by <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> as part of its <i><a href="/wiki/Showcase_(comic_book)" class="mw-redirect" title="Showcase (comic book)">Showcase</a></i> anthology series, in January 1963. This was the first American comic book appearance of James Bond and is noteworthy for being a relatively rare example of a British comic being reprinted in a fairly high-profile American comic. It was also one of the earliest comics to be censored on racial grounds (some skin tones and dialogue were changed for the American market).<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the release of the 1981 film <a href="/wiki/For_Your_Eyes_Only_(film)" title="For Your Eyes Only (film)"><i>For Your Eyes Only</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a> published a two-issue <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> adaptation of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998131_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998131-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompsonFrankenhoffBickford2010368_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompsonFrankenhoffBickford2010368-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> When <i><a href="/wiki/Octopussy" title="Octopussy">Octopussy</a></i> was released in the cinemas in 1983, Marvel published an accompanying comic;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Eclipse also produced a one-off comic for <i>Licence to Kill</i>, although Timothy Dalton refused to allow his likeness to be used.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> New Bond stories were also drawn up and published from 1989 onwards through Marvel, <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_Comics" title="Eclipse Comics">Eclipse Comics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics" title="Dark Horse Comics">Dark Horse Comics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293_111-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConroy2004293-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompsonFrankenhoffBickford2010368_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompsonFrankenhoffBickford2010368-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond in film</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Eon_Productions_films">The Eon Productions films</span></h4>\n<p>In 1962 Eon Productions, the company of Canadian <a href="/wiki/Harry_Saltzman" title="Harry Saltzman">Harry Saltzman</a> and American <a href="/wiki/Albert_R._Broccoli" title="Albert R. Broccoli">Albert R. "Cubby" Broccoli</a>, released the first cinema adaptation of an Ian Fleming novel, <a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)"><i>Dr. No</i></a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> as <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_character)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond (film character)">007</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Connery starred in a further four films before leaving the role after <a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(film)" title="You Only Live Twice (film)"><i>You Only Live Twice</i></a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> which was taken up by <a href="/wiki/George_Lazenby" title="George Lazenby">George Lazenby</a> for <a href="/wiki/On_Her_Majesty%27s_Secret_Service_(film)" title="On Her Majesty&#39;s Secret Service (film)"><i>On Her Majesty\'s Secret Service</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-screenonline_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-screenonline-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Lazenby left the role after just one appearance and Connery was brought back for his last Eon-produced film <a href="/wiki/Diamonds_Are_Forever_(film)" title="Diamonds Are Forever (film)"><i>Diamonds Are Forever</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeeney_Callan2002217_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeeney_Callan2002217-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1973 <a href="/wiki/Roger_Moore" title="Roger Moore">Roger Moore</a> was appointed to the role of 007 for <a href="/wiki/Live_and_Let_Die_(film)" title="Live and Let Die (film)"><i>Live and Let Die</i></a> and played Bond a further six times over twelve years before being replaced by <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Dalton" title="Timothy Dalton">Timothy Dalton</a> for two films. After a six-year hiatus, during which a legal wrangle threatened Eon\'s productions of the Bond films,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson200281_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson200281-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Irish actor <a href="/wiki/Pierce_Brosnan" title="Pierce Brosnan">Pierce Brosnan</a> was cast as Bond in <i><a href="/wiki/GoldenEye" title="GoldenEye">GoldenEye</a></i>, released in 1995; he remained in the role for a total of four films, before leaving in 2002. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Craig" title="Daniel Craig">Daniel Craig</a> was given the role of Bond for <a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)"><i>Casino Royale</i></a>, which rebooted the series.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Craig has appeared for a total of four films and his fifth is scheduled for release in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The series has grossed almost $7 billion to date, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing film series">third-highest-grossing film series</a> (behind <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)"><i>Harry Potter</i></a> and the films of the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Numbers:_Franchises_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Numbers:_Franchises-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> and the single most successful adjusted for inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist:_Potter_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist:_Potter-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="width:240px;">Title\n</th>\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th style="width:110px;">Actor\n</th>\n<th style="width:140px;">Director\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a
