class="mw-redirect" title="Bond 25">Bond 25</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>2020\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Cary_Fukunaga" title="Cary Fukunaga">Cary Fukunaga</a><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-Eon_films">Non-Eon films</span></h4>\n<p>In 1967 <a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(1967_film)" title="Casino Royale (1967 film)"><i>Casino Royale</i></a> was adapted into a <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parody</a> Bond film starring <a href="/wiki/David_Niven" title="David Niven">David Niven</a> as Sir James Bond and <a href="/wiki/Ursula_Andress" title="Ursula Andress">Ursula Andress</a> as Vesper Lynd. Niven had been Fleming\'s preference for the role of Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008202_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008202-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The result of a court case in the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> in London in 1963 allowed <a href="/wiki/Kevin_McClory" title="Kevin McClory">Kevin McClory</a> to produce a remake of <a href="/wiki/Thunderball_(film)" title="Thunderball (film)"><i>Thunderball</i></a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Say_Never_Again" title="Never Say Never Again">Never Say Never Again</a></i> in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-Poliakoff_(2000)_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poliakoff_(2000)-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The film, produced by <a href="/wiki/Jack_Schwartzman" title="Jack Schwartzman">Jack Schwartzman</a>\'s Taliafilm production company and starring Sean Connery as Bond, was not part of the Eon series of Bond films. In 1997 the Sony Corporation acquired all or some of McClory\'s rights in an undisclosed deal,<sup id="cite_ref-Poliakoff_(2000)_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poliakoff_(2000)-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> which were then subsequently acquired by <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">MGM</a>, whilst on 4 December 1997, MGM announced that the company had purchased the rights to <i>Never Say Never Again</i> from Taliafilm.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> As of 2015, Eon holds the full adaptation rights to all of <a href="/wiki/List_of_James_Bond_novels_and_short_stories" title="List of James Bond novels and short stories">Fleming\'s Bond novels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Poliakoff_(2000)_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poliakoff_(2000)-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Title\n</th>\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th>Actor\n</th>\n<th>Director(s)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(1967_film)" title="Casino Royale (1967 film)">Casino Royale</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>1967\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/David_Niven" title="David Niven">David Niven</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ken_Hughes" title="Ken Hughes">Ken Hughes</a><br /><a href="/wiki/John_Huston" title="John Huston">John Huston</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Joseph_McGrath_(film_director)" title="Joseph McGrath (film director)">Joseph McGrath</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Robert_Parrish" title="Robert Parrish">Robert Parrish</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Val_Guest" title="Val Guest">Val Guest</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Richard_Talmadge" title="Richard Talmadge">Richard Talmadge</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Never_Say_Never_Again" title="Never Say Never Again">Never Say Never Again</a></i>\n</td>\n<td>1983\n</td>\n<td>Sean Connery\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Irvin_Kershner" title="Irvin Kershner">Irvin Kershner</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_music" title="James Bond music">James Bond music</a></div>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"...&#160;cocky, swaggering, confident, dark, dangerous, suggestive, sexy, unstoppable."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/David_Arnold" title="David Arnold">David Arnold</a></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a>" was written by <a href="/wiki/Monty_Norman" title="Monty Norman">Monty Norman</a> and was first orchestrated by the <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(composer)" title="John Barry (composer)">John Barry</a> Orchestra for 1962\'s <i>Dr. No</i>, although the actual authorship of the music has been a matter of controversy for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELindner2009122_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELindner2009122-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, Norman won \xc2\xa330,000 in libel damages from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> newspaper, which suggested that Barry was entirely responsible for the composition.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The theme, as written by Norman and arranged by Barry, was described by another Bond film composer, <a href="/wiki/David_Arnold" title="David Arnold">David Arnold</a>, as "bebop-swing vibe coupled with that vicious, dark, distorted electric guitar, definitely an instrument of rock \'n\' roll&#160;... it represented everything about the character you would want: It was cocky, swaggering, confident, dark, dangerous, suggestive, sexy, unstoppable. And he did it in two minutes."<sup id="cite_ref-Burlingame_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burlingame-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Barry composed the <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">scores</a> for eleven Bond films<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChapman200997-98_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChapman200997-98-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> and had an uncredited contribution to <i>Dr. No</i> with his arrangement of the Bond Theme.<sup id="cite_ref-Burlingame_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burlingame-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A Bond film staple are the theme songs heard during their <a href="/wiki/Title_sequence" title="Title sequence">title sequences</a> sung by well-known popular singers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson2002224_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson2002224-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Several of the songs produced for the films have been nominated for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Original Song</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Live_and_Let_Die_(song)" title="Live and Let Die (song)">Live and Let Die</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carly_Simon" title="Carly Simon">Carly Simon</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Nobody_Does_It_Better" title="Nobody Does It Better">Nobody Does It Better</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheena_Easton" title="Sheena Easton">Sheena Easton</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/For_Your_Eyes_Only_(Sheena_Easton_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="For Your Eyes Only (Sheena Easton song)">For Your Eyes Only</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-54th_Oscars_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54th_Oscars-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Skyfall_(Adele_song)" title="Skyfall (Adele song)">Skyfall</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Smith_(singer)" title="Sam Smith (singer)">Sam Smith</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Writing%27s_on_the_Wall_(Sam_Smith_song)" title="Writing&#39;s on the Wall (Sam Smith song)">Writing\'s on the Wall</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Adele won the award at the <a href="/wiki/85th_Academy_Awards" title="85th Academy Awards">85th Academy Awards</a>, and Smith won at the <a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">88th Academy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> For the non-Eon produced <i>Casino Royale</i>, <a href="/wiki/Burt_Bacharach" title="Burt Bacharach">Burt Bacharach</a>\'s score included "<a href="/wiki/The_Look_of_Love_(1967_song)" title="The Look of Love (1967 song)">The Look of Love</a>", which was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Song" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Best Song">Academy Award for Best Song</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40th_Oscars_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40th_Oscars-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_video_games" title="James Bond in video games">James Bond in video games</a></div>\n<p>In 1983 the first Bond video game, developed and published by <a href="/wiki/Parker_Brothers" title="Parker Brothers">Parker Brothers</a>, was released for the <a href="/wiki/Atari_2600" title="Atari 2600">Atari 2600</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atari_5200" title="Atari 5200">Atari 5200</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atari_800" class="mw-redirect" title="Atari 800">Atari 800</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commodore_64" title="Commodore 64">Commodore 64</a> and the <a href="/wiki/ColecoVision" title="ColecoVision">ColecoVision</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Since then, there have been numerous video games either based on the films or using original storylines. In 1997 the <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> <a href="/wiki/GoldenEye_007_(1997_video_game)" title="GoldenEye 007 (1997 video game)"><i>GoldenEye 007</i></a> was developed by <a href="/wiki/Rare_(company)" title="Rare (company)">Rare</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_64" title="Nintendo 64">Nintendo 64</a>, based on the 1995 Pierce Brosnan film <i><a href="/wiki/GoldenEye" title="GoldenEye">GoldenEye</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gaming_Age_review_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaming_Age_review-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The game received very positive reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> won the BAFTA Interactive Entertainment Award for UK Developer of the Year in 1998<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> and sold over eight million copies worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-hollis-speech_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollis-speech-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Microsoft-Rare_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Microsoft-Rare-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> grossing $250 million.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> acquired the licence and released <a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Dies_(video_game)" title="Tomorrow Never Dies (video game)"><i>Tomorrow Never Dies</i></a> on 16 December 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In October 2000, they released <a href="/wiki/007:_The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(Nintendo_64)" class="mw-redirect" title="007: The World Is Not Enough (Nintendo 64)"><i>The World Is Not Enough</i></a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKingKrzywinska2002183_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKingKrzywinska2002183-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_64" title="Nintendo 64">Nintendo 64</a><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> followed by <i>007 Racing</i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a> on 21 November 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, the company released <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_007:_Everything_or_Nothing" title="James Bond 007: Everything or Nothing">James Bond 007: Everything or Nothing</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> which included the likenesses and voices of Pierce Brosnan, <a href="/wiki/Willem_Dafoe" title="Willem Dafoe">Willem Dafoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidi_Klum" title="Heidi Klum">Heidi Klum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judi_Dench" title="Judi Dench">Judi Dench</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">John Cleese</a>, amongst others.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In November 2005, Electronic Arts released a video game adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/007:_From_Russia_with_Love" class="mw-redirect" title="007: From Russia with Love">007: From Russia with Love</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FRWL_IGN_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRWL_IGN-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> which involved Sean Connery\'s image and voice-over for Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-FRWL_IGN_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRWL_IGN-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In 2006 Electronic Arts announced a game based on then-upcoming film <i>Casino Royale</i>: the game was cancelled because it would not be ready by the film\'s release in November of that year. With MGM losing revenue from lost licensing fees, the franchise was removed from EA to <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Activision subsequently released the <i><a href="/wiki/007:_Quantum_of_Solace" title="007: Quantum of Solace">007: Quantum of Solace</a></i> game on 31 October 2008, based on the film of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new version of <a href="/wiki/GoldenEye_007_(2010_video_game)" title="GoldenEye 007 (2010 video game)"><i>GoldenEye 007</i></a> featuring Daniel Craig was released for the <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> and a handheld version for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> in November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> A year later a new version was released for <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> under the title <i><a href="/wiki/GoldenEye_007:_Reloaded" class="mw-redirect" title="GoldenEye 007: Reloaded">GoldenEye 007: Reloaded</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In October 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/007_Legends" title="007 Legends">007 Legends</a></i> was released, which featured one mission from each of the Bond actors of the Eon Productions\' series.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Guns.2C_vehicles_and_gadgets"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Guns,_vehicles_and_gadgets">Guns, vehicles and gadgets</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_James_Bond_vehicles" title="List of James Bond vehicles">List of James Bond vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_James_Bond_gadgets" title="List of James Bond gadgets">List of James Bond gadgets</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guns">Guns</span></h3>\n<p>For the first five novels, Fleming armed Bond with a <a href="/wiki/Beretta_418" title="Beretta 418">Beretta 418</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson1988265_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson1988265-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> until he received a letter from a thirty-one-year-old Bond enthusiast and gun expert, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Boothroyd" title="Geoffrey Boothroyd">Geoffrey Boothroyd</a>, criticising Fleming\'s choice of firearm for Bond,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor2005160_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor2005160-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> calling it "a lady\'s gun \xe2\x80\x93 and not a very nice lady at that!"<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Boothroyd suggested that Bond should swap his <a href="/wiki/Beretta" title="Beretta">Beretta</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Walther_PP" title="Walther PP">Walther PP</a>K 7.65mm and this exchange of arms made it to <i>Dr. No</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008132_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008132-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Boothroyd also gave Fleming advice on the <a href="/wiki/Berns-Martin" title="Berns-Martin">Berns-Martin</a> triple draw shoulder holster and a number of the weapons used by SMERSH and other villains.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198815_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198815-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> In thanks, Fleming gave the MI6 Armourer in his novels the name Major Boothroyd and, in <i>Dr. No</i>, M introduces him to Bond as "the greatest small-arms expert in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008132_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacintyre2008132-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Bond also used a variety of <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Savage_Model_99" title="Savage Model 99">Savage Model 99</a> in "For Your Eyes Only" and a Winchester .308 target rifle in "The Living Daylights".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson1988265_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson1988265-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Other handguns used by Bond in the Fleming books included the <a href="/wiki/Colt_Detective_Special" title="Colt Detective Special">Colt Detective Special</a> and a long-barrelled <a href="/wiki/Colt_Single_Action_Army" title="Colt Single Action Army">Colt .45 Army Special</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson1988265_162-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson1988265-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Bond film, <i>Dr. No</i>, saw M ordering Bond to leave his Beretta behind and take up the Walther PPK,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack200594_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack200594-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> which the film Bond used in eighteen films.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007265_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007265-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Tomorrow Never Dies</i> and the two subsequent films, Bond\'s main weapon was the <a href="/wiki/Walther_P99" title="Walther P99">Walther P99</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_pistol" title="Semi-automatic pistol">semi-automatic pistol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007265_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007265-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aston.db5.coupe.300pix.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Aston.db5.coupe.300pix.jpg/220px-Aston.db5.coupe.300pix.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d3/Aston.db5.coupe.300pix.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="214" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aston.db5.coupe.300pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DB5" title="Aston Martin DB5">Aston Martin DB5</a> as seen in <i><a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(film)" title="Goldfinger (film)">Goldfinger</a></i>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vehicles">Vehicles</span></h3>\n<p>In the early Bond stories Fleming gave Bond a battleship-grey <a href="/wiki/Bentley_4%C2%BD_Litre" title="Bentley 4\xc2\xbd Litre">Bentley 4\xc2\xbd Litre</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Amherst_Villiers" title="Amherst Villiers">Amherst Villiers</a> <a href="/wiki/Supercharger" title="Supercharger">supercharger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198862-63_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198862-63-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> After Bond\'s car was written off by Hugo Drax in <i>Moonraker</i>, Fleming gave Bond a Mark II Continental Bentley, which he used in the remaining books of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198863_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198863-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> During <i>Goldfinger</i>, Bond was issued with an <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DB_Mark_III" title="Aston Martin DB Mark III">Aston Martin DB Mark III</a> with a homing device, which he used to track Goldfinger across France. Bond returned to his Bentley for the subsequent novels.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198863_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198863-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Bond of the films has driven a number of cars, including the <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_V8_Vantage_(1977)" title="Aston Martin V8 Vantage (1977)">Aston Martin V8 Vantage</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007183_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007183-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> during the 1980s, the <a href="/wiki/V12_Vanquish" class="mw-redirect" title="V12 Vanquish">V12 Vanquish</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007183_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007183-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DBS_V12" title="Aston Martin DBS V12">DBS</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007182_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007182-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> during the 2000s, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Esprit" title="Lotus Esprit">Lotus Esprit</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007202_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007202-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/BMW_Z3" title="BMW Z3">BMW Z3</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007186_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007186-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BMW_750iL" class="mw-redirect" title="BMW 750iL">BMW 750iL</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007186_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007186-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/BMW_Z8" title="BMW Z8">BMW Z8</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007186_174-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007186-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> He has, however, also needed to drive a number of other vehicles, ranging from a <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_2CV" title="Citro\xc3\xabn 2CV">Citro\xc3\xabn 2CV</a> to a <a href="/wiki/AEC_Routemaster" title="AEC Routemaster">Routemaster</a> Bus, amongst others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007175_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007175-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bond\'s most famous car is the silver grey <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin_DB5" title="Aston Martin DB5">Aston Martin DB5</a>, first seen in <i>Goldfinger</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007180_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007180-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> it later featured in <i>Thunderball</i>, <i>GoldenEye</i>, <i>Tomorrow Never Dies</i>, <i>Casino Royale</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Skyfall" title="Skyfall">Skyfall</a></i> and <i>Spectre</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007180-181_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007180-181-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Obs:_french_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obs:_french-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The films have used a number of different Aston Martins for filming and publicity, one of which was sold in January 2006 at an auction in the US for $2,1 million to an unnamed European collector.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>In 2010, another DB5 used in Goldfinger was sold at auction for $4.6m million (\xc2\xa32.6 million).<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gadgets">Gadgets</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Little_Nellie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Small, one man, open-cockpit helicopter on a lawn about the size of a car next to it, with a man sitting in it." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Little_Nellie.jpg/220px-Little_Nellie.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Little_Nellie.jpg/330px-Little_Nellie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Little_Nellie.jpg/440px-Little_Nellie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2287" data-file-height="1496" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Little_Nellie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i>Little Nellie</i> autogyro with its creator and pilot, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Wallis" title="Ken Wallis">Ken Wallis</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Fleming\'s novels and early screen adaptations presented minimal equipment such as the booby-trapped <a href="/wiki/Attach%C3%A9_case" class="mw-redirect" title="Attach\xc3\xa9 case">attach\xc3\xa9 case</a> in <i>From Russia with Love</i>, although this situation changed dramatically with the films.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> However, the effects of the two Eon-produced Bond films <i>Dr. No</i> and <i>From Russia with Love</i> had an effect on the novel <i>The Man with the Golden Gun</i>, through the increased number of devices used in Fleming\'s final story.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChancellor2005234_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChancellor2005234-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the film adaptations of Bond, the pre-mission briefing by Q Branch became one of the motifs that ran through the series.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELindner2009112_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELindner2009112-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dr. No</i> provided no spy-related gadgets, but a <a href="/wiki/Geiger_counter" title="Geiger counter">Geiger counter</a> was used; industrial designer Andy Davey observed that the first ever onscreen spy-gadget was the attach\xc3\xa9 case shown in <i>From Russia with Love</i>, which he described as "a classic 007 product".<sup id="cite_ref-Davey_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davey-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The gadgets assumed a higher profile in the 1964 film <i>Goldfinger</i>. The film\'s success encouraged further espionage equipment from Q Branch to be supplied to Bond, although the increased use of technology led to an accusation that Bond was over-reliant on equipment, particularly in the later films.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELindner2009169_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELindner2009169-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:20em;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"If it hadn\'t been for Q Branch, you\'d have been dead long ago!"</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Q, to Bond, <i>Licence to Kill</i></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Davey noted that "Bond\'s gizmos follow the <a href="/wiki/Zeitgeist" title="Zeitgeist">zeitgeist</a> more closely than any other&#160;... nuance in the films"<sup id="cite_ref-Davey_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davey-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> as they moved from the potential representations of the future in the early films, through to the brand-name obsessions of the later films.<sup id="cite_ref-Davey_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davey-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> It is also noticeable that, although Bond uses a number of pieces of equipment from Q Branch, including the Little Nellie <a href="/wiki/Autogyro" title="Autogyro">autogyro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007200-201_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007200-201-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Jet_pack#Bell_Textron_Rocket_Belt" title="Jet pack">jet pack</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting2007128_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting2007128-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> and the exploding attach\xc3\xa9 case,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007221_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkStutz2007221-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> the villains are also well-equipped with custom-made devices,<sup id="cite_ref-Davey_184-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davey-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> including Scaramanga\'s golden gun,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting200777_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJ\xc3\xbctting200777-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Rosa Klebb\'s poison-tipped shoes,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriswold200641_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriswold200641-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Oddjob\'s steel-rimmed bowler hat<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2005117_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2005117-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> and Blofeld\'s communication devices in his agents\' vanity case.<sup id="cite_ref-Davey_184-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davey-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_impact">Cultural impact</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_James_Bond_parodies_and_spin-offs" title="List of James Bond parodies and spin-offs">List of James Bond parodies and spin-offs</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg/170px-Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg/255px-Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg/340px-Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="429" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fleming%27s_paperback_Bonds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fleming\'s Bond novels</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Bond_Island.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/James_Bond_Island.JPG/220px-James_Bond_Island.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/James_Bond_Island.JPG/330px-James_Bond_Island.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/James_Bond_Island.JPG/440px-James_Bond_Island.JPG 2x" data-file-width="912" data-file-height="684" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Bond_Island.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>James Bond Island (<a href="/wiki/Khao_Phing_Kan" title="Khao Phing Kan">Khao Phing Kan</a>, Thailand)</div></div></div>\n<p>Cinematically, Bond has been a major influence within the spy genre since the release of <i>Dr. No</i> in 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithLavington200221_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithLavington200221-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> with 22 secret agent films released in 1966 alone attempting to capitalise on the Bond franchise\'s popularity and success.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The first parody was the 1964 film <i><a href="/wiki/Carry_On_Spying" title="Carry On Spying">Carry On Spying</a></i>, which shows the villain Dr. Crow being overcome by agents who included James Bind (<a href="/wiki/Charles_Hawtrey_(actor_born_1914)" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Hawtrey (actor born 1914)">Charles Hawtry</a>) and Daphne Honeybutt (<a href="/wiki/Barbara_Windsor" title="Barbara Windsor">Barbara Windsor</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> One of the films that reacted against the portrayal of Bond was the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Palmer" title="Harry Palmer">Harry Palmer</a> series, whose first film, <a href="/wiki/The_Ipcress_File_(film)" title="The Ipcress File (film)"><i>The Ipcress File</i></a> was released in 1965. The eponymous hero of the series was what academic Jeremy Packer called an "anti-Bond",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPacker200926_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPacker200926-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> or what Christoph Lindner calls "the thinking man\'s Bond".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELindner2009128_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELindner2009128-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The Palmer series were produced by Harry Saltzman, who also used key crew members from the Bond series, including designer <a href="/wiki/Ken_Adam" title="Ken Adam">Ken Adam</a>, editor <a href="/wiki/Peter_R._Hunt" title="Peter R. Hunt">Peter R. Hunt</a> and composer John Barry.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The four "<a href="/wiki/Matt_Helm" title="Matt Helm">Matt Helm</a>" films starring <a href="/wiki/Dean_Martin" title="Dean Martin">Dean Martin</a> (released between 1966 and 1969),<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> the "<a href="/wiki/Our_Man_Flint" title="Our Man Flint">Flint</a>" series starring <a href="/wiki/James_Coburn" title="James Coburn">James Coburn</a> (comprising two films, one each in 1966 and 1969),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998210_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998210-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_from_U.N.C.L.E." title="The Man from U.N.C.L.E.">The Man from U.N.C.L.E.</a></i> also moved onto the cinema screen, with eight films released: all were testaments to Bond\'s prominence in popular culture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChapman200997-98_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChapman200997-98-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> More recently, the <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Austin Powers (film series)">Austin Powers</a></i> series by writer, producer and comedian <a href="/wiki/Mike_Myers" title="Mike Myers">Mike Myers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELindner200976_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELindner200976-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> and other parodies such as the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/Johnny_English" title="Johnny English">Johnny English</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> have also used elements from or parodied the Bond films.\n</p><p>Following the release of the film <i>Dr. No</i> in 1962, the line "Bond&#160;... James Bond", became a <a href="/wiki/Catch_phrase" class="mw-redirect" title="Catch phrase">catch phrase</a> that entered the <a href="/wiki/Lexicon" title="Lexicon">lexicon</a> of Western popular culture: writers Cork and Scivally said of the introduction in <i>Dr. No</i> that the "signature introduction would become the most famous and loved film line ever".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECorkScivally20026_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECorkScivally20026-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, it was voted as the "best-loved one-liner in cinema" by British cinema goers,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> and in 2005, it was honoured as the 22nd greatest quotation in cinema history by the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> as part of their <a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years..._100_Movie_Quotes" class="mw-redirect" title="AFI&#39;s 100 Years... 100 Movie Quotes">100 Years Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The 2005 <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a>\'s \'100 Years\' series recognised the character of James Bond himself as the <a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years..._100_Heroes_and_Villains" class="mw-redirect" title="AFI&#39;s 100 Years... 100 Heroes and Villains">third greatest film hero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> He was also placed at number 11 on a similar list by <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> and as the fifth greatest movie character of all time by <a href="/wiki/Premiere_(magazine)" title="Premiere (magazine)"><i>Premiere</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 23 James Bond films produced by Eon Productions, which have grossed $4,910 million in box office returns alone,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> have made the series one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing film series">highest-grossing ever</a>. It is estimated that since <i>Dr. No</i>, a quarter of the world\'s population have seen at least one Bond film.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The UK Film Distributors\' Association have stated that the importance of the Bond series of films to the British film industry cannot be overstated, as they "form the backbone of the industry".<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Television also saw the effect of Bond films, with the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_from_U.N.C.L.E." title="The Man from U.N.C.L.E.">The Man from U.N.C.L.E.</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> which was described as the "first network television imitation" of Bond,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> largely because Fleming provided advice and ideas on the development of the series, even giving the main character the name <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Solo" title="Napoleon Solo">Napoleon Solo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998209_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998209-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Other 1960s television series inspired by Bond include <i><a href="/wiki/I_Spy_(1965_TV_series)" title="I Spy (1965 TV series)">I Spy</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998210_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998210-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Smart" title="Get Smart">Get Smart</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998211_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPfeifferWorrall1998211-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British cultural icon</a>, by 2012, James Bond had become such a symbol of the United Kingdom that the character, played by Craig, appeared in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 London Olympics</a> as Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>\'s escort.<sup id="cite_ref-brown20120727_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brown20120727-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout the life of the film series, a number of <a href="/wiki/Merchandising" title="Merchandising">tie-in products</a> have been released.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimpson2002273_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimpson2002273-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 a James Bond museum opened atop of Austrian Alps.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Futuristic" class="mw-redirect" title="Futuristic">futuristic</a> museum is constructed on the summit of Gaislachkogl Mountain in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6lden" title="S\xc3\xb6lden">S\xc3\xb6lden</a> at 3,048 m above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms_of_James_Bond">Criticisms of James Bond</span></h2>\n<p>The James Bond character and related media have triggered a number of criticisms and reactions across the political spectrum, and are still highly debated in <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture_studies" title="Popular culture studies">popular culture studies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Some observers accuse the Bond novels and films of <a href="/wiki/Misogyny" title="Misogyny">misogyny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Geographers have considered the role of exotic locations in the movies in the dynamics of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, with power struggles among blocs playing out in the peripheral areas.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Other critics claim that the Bond films reflect <a href="/wiki/Nostalgia" title="Nostalgia">imperial nostalgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> American conservative critics, particularly in the 1960s and 1970s, saw Bond as a <a href="/wiki/Nihilism" title="Nihilism">nihilistic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedonism" title="Hedonism">hedonistic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amorality" title="Amorality">amoral</a> character that challenged <a href="/wiki/Family_values" title="Family values">family values</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist
